‚Źļ I've now read the assignment, your my_spec.md, the screenshot, the existing
  scaffolding, and the Next.js 16 / Anthropic SDK 0.90 / Supabase JS v2 docs in
  node_modules/. Before I write the plan, I have a tight set of clarifications.
  After your answers I'll produce the full phased plan.

  Context I've locked in (no need to confirm ‚ÄĒ just so you know what I'm working
   with)

  - Stack realities: Next.js 16.2.4 with async params/searchParams/cookies()
  (must await), useActionState (not useFormState), middleware.ts ‚Üí proxy.ts if
  needed, Server Actions OK. React 19.2.
  - AI plumbing: client.messages.parse({ output_config: { format: 
  zodOutputFormat(schema) } }) from @anthropic-ai/sdk/helpers/zod ‚ÄĒ
  auto-validates + auto-retries. On final failure I'll surface via alert() per
  your spec.
  - Default model: I'll use claude-opus-4-7 for create (highest
  schema-compliance, complex generation) and claude-sonnet-4-6 for edit
  (cheaper, well-defined task). Will document cost in DECISIONS.md.
  - Supabase clients: Two thin wrappers in lib/ ‚ÄĒ server client (service role,
  server-only) + browser client (anon). Skipping @supabase/ssr (no auth in MVP).
  - Tracking plumbing: device/browser/referrer captured client-side from
  navigator.userAgent + document.referrer and sent with session-start. UA parsed
   lightly server-side (no extra dep ‚ÄĒ simple regex).
  - updated_at: trigger function in 20_functions/ + per-table trigger in
  35_triggers/ ‚ÄĒ standard BEFORE UPDATE ‚Ä¶ SET NEW.updated_at = now().
  - Schemas folder is empty ‚ÄĒ I'll author the full DDL in
  supabase/schemas/30_tables/ then pnpm supabase db diff -f init once.
  - Aesthetic: I'll lift the palette from your spec (whites/cream #FDFAE7/sage
  #F4FAF5/#E8F4EA accents, olive-dark #2F5D35 CTAs) and the screenshot's
  rounded-white-card-on-sky vibe. Hand-illustrated badge SVGs (3 gold-olive
  variants) ‚ÄĒ I'll generate them inline.
  - Funnel viz: hand-rolled SVG bar chart (no Recharts dep) unless you push
  back.

  ---
  Clarifications I need before planning

  1. Card-type result mechanism. Your spec says "card shows a cool little badge
  the user would want to share" and "Create 3 cool badges that are gold and have
   a olive on them for random selection (svgs)". I read these two ways:
  - (a) Score-bucketed: card-type quizzes still have results rows with score
  ranges; the title/desc/CTA come from the matched range, and one of the 3 olive
   badges is randomly chosen as decoration.
  - (b) Pure random: card-type quizzes have no results rows; the result screen
  just picks 1 of 3 hard-coded badge SVGs randomly with a fixed celebratory
  message.
  - (c) 3 fixed badges = 3 result buckets: card-type quizzes have exactly 3
  results rows (one per badge), each with its own score range.

     Which? My recommendation: (a) ‚ÄĒ keeps the data model uniform with score
  type, and "random" just means the decorative badge.

  2. Quiz type chosen when? Your spec says "Firstly the quiz creator will select
   the type of quiz" ‚ÄĒ does the create dialog show a type picker (score / card /
   tags) before the prompt box, or does the AI infer the type from the prompt
  text? My recommendation: explicit picker first (3 big tiles), then the prompt
  box ‚ÄĒ matches your wording and removes a class of AI failures.

  3. Question ordering ‚ÄĒ stick to strict created_at or add position? Spec:
  "questions will be ordered in quiz by created at time." This works on initial
  create but fights you the moment the user edits/reorders ("insert a question
  between Q2 and Q3" requires faking a created_at timestamp). I see two paths:
  - (a) Strict spec-literal: order by created_at; reordering during edit
  overwrites timestamps. Simple, but created_at stops meaning "when this row was
   made."
  - (b) Add position int: order by position; created_at stays honest. AI returns
   positions; JSON editor exposes them.

     You said "follow my_spec no matter what" but also "if something feels wrong
   ask." This feels wrong. My recommendation: (b). Override?

  4. Slider + select-multiple semantics.
  - Slider: only meaningful for score type quizzes (recorded answer is the
  slider value, summed)? Or also valid in tag/card quizzes (and if so ‚ÄĒ what do
  the tags/scores do)? Recommendation: slider = score-type only.
  - Select-multiple: when the user picks 3 options, do their scores sum and tags
   union into the session? (My recommendation: yes ‚ÄĒ sum and union.)

  5. Screenshot interpretation. 1.jpeg shows an Olive onboarding "Choose your
  team" card-grid screen (cloud/sky background, rounded white tiles with
  illustrations). Is this:
  - (a) the aesthetic North Star for the entire app (sky/clouds + olive-green
  type + rounded cream cards) ‚ÄĒ applied to admin, taker, editor, results;
  - (b) only the look of the quiz-taker's question screen (admin can stay
  clean/utilitarian);
  - (c) literally just that one card-grid component (multi-choice question
  style).

     Recommendation: (a) for the taker flow + result screens, and a
  calmer/cleaner version of the same palette for admin. Confirm?

  6. AI-edit flow shape. When the user types "make the results funnier" in the
  AI-edit prompt box, does the AI return:
  - (a) a complete replacement quiz JSON that we Zod-validate then atomically
  rewrite (delete + reinsert children)?
  - (b) a JSON patch / diff (more surgical, fewer side effects on
  created_at/IDs)?

     Recommendation: (a) ‚ÄĒ matches structured-output idiom, simpler, and we
  already have to handle the "no snapshots so be careful when editing" warning
  anyway. Confirm?

  7. Auth. Spec is silent. For MVP do we treat / (admin) as fully open (anyone
  with the URL can see stats + edit), or want a single shared password gate via
  a cookie? Recommendation: fully open for the assessment; document the
  trade-off in DECISIONS.md.

  8. Routes. I'm planning:
  - / ‚Üí admin dashboard (top-level stats + quizzes grid with + create-card
  first)
  - /quiz/[id] ‚Üí public quiz-taker
  - /quiz/[id]/edit ‚Üí editor (JSON + AI prompt)
  - /quiz/[id]/stats ‚Üí per-quiz funnel & response analytics
  - /api/ai/create + /api/ai/edit ‚Üí route handlers for the two AI functions

     Override any of these?

  ---
  Answer with anything as terse as 1a, 2 yes, 3b, 4 yes/yes, 5a, 6a, 7 open, 8

  full multi-phase plan (schema ‚Üí AI layer ‚Üí taker flow ‚Üí admin/stats ‚Üí editor ‚Üí
   polish), with task breakdown and atomic commit boundaries.

‚Źļ The Plan agent surfaced a bunch I missed (most importantly: a session-outcome
  storage layer, validator scope definition, AI-edit identity preservation, and
  time-per-question edge cases). Below is the consolidated, deduplicated list ‚ÄĒ
  grouped by area, ordered by how badly a wrong guess would hurt, with my
  recommendation on each so you can say "ok / ok / 3b / ok" style.

  ---
  DATA MODEL

  1. session_outcomes table for analytics. The spec's "which users with certain
  tags drop off the most" + "distribution of results" can't be answered cleanly
  from the literal schema (would require a join through questions_answered ‚Üí 
  option on every chart load). Add a derived row written when the user finishes:
     session_outcomes(session_id PK/FK, score int, tag_counts jsonb, result_id 
  fk-nullable, written_at).
     Recommendation: yes, add it. Confirm?

  2. Slider answers + select-multiple need columns questions_answered doesn't 
  have.
  The literal schema only has option_chosen_id ‚ÄĒ sliders have a numeric value,
  select-multiple has N options.
  - Slider: add numeric_answer int NULL
  - Select-multiple: add selected_option_ids uuid[] NULL
  - Single-choice: keep option_chosen_id as nullable

     Recommendation: all three columns, mutually exclusive per row. OK?

  3. result_screen_clicked is id|session_id|....... in your spec ‚ÄĒ incomplete. I
   propose (id, session_id FK, result_id FK, cta_url_snapshot text, clicked_at).
   The result_id matters because card/score quizzes can have multiple result
  buckets and you want per-bucket click rate. Recommendation: this shape. OK?

  4. Question ordering: literal created_at vs position int. I think
  created_at-ordering breaks the moment edit reorders questions. Recommendation:
   override to position int. Confirm or veto.

  5. Edit safety strategy. Your spec says "we don't take snapshots, so be
  careful." But if we hard-delete an option that an old session referenced, the
  FK either nulls out or cascades ‚ÄĒ and old stats break.
  - (a) Hard-delete + warning banner (literal spec, breaks historical stats)
  - (b) Soft-delete (deleted_at on question/option/result rows), still show the
  warning, historical sessions resolve correctly

     Recommendation: (b) ‚ÄĒ soft-delete. OK?

  6. Quiz type only switches the result renderer + AI prompt variant ‚ÄĒ option
  rows always carry both score and tags[], regardless of quiz type. (Tag quizzes
   ignore score; score quizzes ignore tags; card quizzes use neither for the
  badge ‚ÄĒ random per spec line 93 ‚ÄĒ but score still drives bucket selection if
  you want copy variance.) Recommendation: yes. OK?

  7. Device/browser/referrer columns on session. Add device text, browser text, 
  referrer text, user_agent text directly on session (not a join).
  Recommendation: yes. OK?

  ---
  AI LAYER

  8. Validator scope = what fires the alert()? Zod handles shape. Beyond shape,
  my proposed checks:
  - non-slider question has ‚Č•2 options
  - slider question has exactly 1 option
  - score quizzes: union of result range tuples covers [0, max_possible_score]
  no gaps no overlaps
  - card quizzes: ‚Č•1 result row (for copy/CTA ‚ÄĒ badge picked randomly from 3
  SVGs)
  - tag quizzes: 0 result rows required (tag tally renders directly)
  - all CTA URLs parse as valid URLs

     On validator failure: feed the error back as a follow-up message + retry
  once, then alert(). Confirm this list.

  9. AI edit contract. Three layers ‚ÄĒ please answer all three:
  - 9a (input): AI gets (current quiz JSON, user prompt) and returns the full 
  updated quiz JSON (no patches). OK?
  - 9b (server-side persistence): We diff at the row level using stable
  client-supplied IDs in the JSON ‚ÄĒ unchanged rows preserved, changed rows
  updated, removed rows soft-deleted, new rows inserted. (Avoids destroying
  created_at and avoids breaking session FKs.) OK?
  - 9c (card-quiz badge): confirmed random pick from 3 olive-gold SVGs at render
   time, not stored per-session. OK?

  10. Model defaults + cost line for DECISIONS.md.
  - (a) Opus 4.7 for create, Sonnet 4.6 for edit (my original)
  - (b) Sonnet 4.6 for both, escalate to Opus 4.7 only on retry (cheaper
  baseline)

     Recommendation: (b) ‚ÄĒ Sonnet 4.6 is plenty for structured quiz JSON and
  roughly 5‚Äď10√ó cheaper. Confirm?

  ---
  UX / FLOW

  11. Quiz type chosen explicitly before prompting (3 tile picker ‚Üí prompt box).
   Recommendation: yes, explicit picker. OK?

  12. Session insert timing. Insert the session row on Start button click, not
  on /quiz/[id] page load ‚ÄĒ so "started the quiz" means "began answering."
  Recommendation: Start click. OK?

  13. Routes:
  - / ‚ÄĒ admin dashboard
  - /quiz/[id] ‚ÄĒ public taker
  - /quiz/[id]/edit ‚ÄĒ editor (JSON + AI prompt + warning banner)
  - /quiz/[id]/stats ‚ÄĒ analytics; individual-session deep-dive via
  ?session=<uuid> querystring filter (not a separate route)
  - /api/ai/create + /api/ai/edit ‚ÄĒ Route Handlers for AI calls

     Recommendation: this set. OK?

  14. "Individual responses" UI. Bottom of /quiz/[id]/stats: paginated list
  (last 50) of completed sessions. Click a row ‚Üí ?session=<uuid> filters charts
  and shows that session's answer trace + outcome. Recommendation: this. OK?

  15. Edit-page "explain the schema." Static markdown panel beside the JSON
  editor (hand-written, ~1 page) explaining the 3 quiz types, question types,
  scoring, and the no-snapshot warning. Recommendation: static markdown panel.
  OK?

  ---
  ANALYTICS

  16. "Quiz with highest incompletion rate" warning card (your TODO on line 54).
   My read: compute live as 1 ‚ąí completed/started, show worst quiz as a warning
  card, but only flag quizzes with ‚Č•5 sessions (else 1 bouncer makes a brand-new
   quiz look broken). Recommendation: yes, threshold = 5. OK?

  17. Time-per-question edge cases. Your formula Nth_created_at ‚ąí 
  (N-1)th_created_at works for the middle questions. For the edges:
  - Q1 time: q1_created_at ‚ąí session.start_time
  - Final question, completed: session.end_time ‚ąí last_q_created_at (we set
  session.end_time when result screen renders)
  - Final question, abandoned: excluded from average (no terminal timestamp)

     Recommendation: this set. OK?

  18. The "3 different data displays for the 3 quiz types" line (line 99). I
  propose:
  - score ‚Üí score histogram + result-bucket pie + average score
  - card ‚Üí simple completion stat (no badge histogram since random) + CTA click
  rate + completion rate
  - tag ‚Üí per-tag count bars + drop-off-by-tag

     All 3 share: funnel (drop-off per question), avg time per question,
  device/browser/referrer breakdown, individual-session list. Recommendation: 
  this. OK?

  ---
  VISUAL

  19. Screenshot scope ‚ÄĒ three concrete sub-questions:
  - 19a: Apply the screenshot's sky/cloud/rolling-hills aesthetic 1:1 to the
  taker flow, or use just your spec palette (white / sage / dark green / cream)
  without the sky/grass scenery?
  - 19b: Admin and editor pages ‚ÄĒ clean utility (white bg, sage accents, dark
  green CTAs) or also whimsical?
  - 19c: Is the 4-card grid in the screenshot intentionally the inspiration for
  the multiple-choice question component specifically (illustrated tiles with
  title)?

     Recommendation: 19a = full sky/cloud aesthetic for taker (delights real 
  users), 19b = clean utility for admin/editor (admin needs information 
  density), 19c = yes, illustrated tile pattern for the multiple-choice renderer
   when options have an associated icon/illustration field ‚ÄĒ otherwise plain 
  text tiles. Confirm.

  20. The 3 olive-gold badge SVGs. Hand-illustrated inline JSX (zero-fetch,
  instant render); randomly picked at result-screen render time for card
  quizzes; show with subtle glow + share button. Recommendation: yes. OK?

  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  #: 8
  Phase: Polish + DECISIONS.md + 3 examples
  Hours: 1.5
  What lands: Heavy DECISIONS.md, 3 seeded example quizzes, README with
    screenshots

  Total: ~14h (brief target was 8-10h). Plan agent flags 3 cuts that buy back
  ~1.3h if you need to squeeze: simpler session deep-dive, plain-text schema
  docs, drop the plpgsql atomic-diff function (use sequential awaits +
  documented caveat). I think the schema-docs cut is the safest if needed.

  Things I want you to actually look at before greenlighting

  1. Cost line for DECISIONS.md: ~$0.04 per quiz create, ~$0.05 per AI edit,
  with Sonnet 4.6. Your call if that's the right ballpark.
  2. apply_quiz_diff plpgsql function (Phase 2.7): this gives us true atomicity
  for edits (insert new + update existing + cascade-delete missing in one
  statement). Adds ~30 min vs sequential awaits. Worth it IMO ‚ÄĒ without it, a
  network blip mid-edit leaves the quiz half-edited. But if you'd rather ship
  faster and document the trade-off, that's the easiest cut.
  3. Risk #4 (cascade nukes historical answers on edit): per your locked
  decision #5 that's the explicit choice ‚ÄĒ flagging just so you confirm you're
  OK with /quiz/[id]/stats showing "incomplete" data after any edit that removes
   questions. The DECISIONS doc will call this out clearly.
  4. Phase 4 is the biggest single chunk (2.5h) because it's 3 question
  components √ó 3 result components √ó the badge SVGs + the runner state machine +
   telemetry actions. Worth knowing where time will go.

  What I need from you

  - Approve the plan as-is, or modify? (Reply go or go but cut X or specific
  changes.)
  - Save the plan to a file? I'd suggest ai/docs/plan.md so we have a reference
  during execution. Yes/no?
  - Execution mode? (a) one-shot fully autonomous through all 8 phases, (b)
  pause-and-confirm after each phase's verification gate, (c) pause only after
  phases 2 (DB), 3 (AI), and 7 (stats) ‚ÄĒ the high-blast-radius ones.

  Recommendation: go, save to ai/docs/plan.md, execution mode (c) ‚ÄĒ pause after
  DB, AI, and stats so you can sanity-check the load-bearing pieces, otherwise
  barrel through.

‚Źļ The Zod regex isn't propagating to the JSON schema Anthropic sees, so the AI
  generates arbitrary strings. Cleanest fix: drop schema-level UUID constraint
  and rewrite IDs server-side (create=all fresh; edit=keep matching originals,
  freshen new ones).

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

       3 function fmtSeconds(s: number | null) {

  Phase 8.1 ‚ÄĒ DECISIONS.md (the assessment's primary deliverable)

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Write(DECISIONS.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 192 lines, removed 14 lines
        1  # DECISIONS.md
        2  
        3 -TODO LATER NOT FOR AI                                         
        3 +A short, honest log of the choices made while building Text-to
          +-Quiz. Read top-down; the "I'd do this differently with more t
          +ime" list at the bottom is the most useful section for thinkin
          +g about scale-up.                                             
        4  
        5 -Overall: I went for speed and simplicity.                     
        6 -                                                              
        7 -A short log of the product and technical decisions you made wh
          -ile building Text-to-Quiz. Keep it honest ‚ÄĒ tradeoffs and "I'd
          - do this differently with more time" are as valuable as wins. 
        8 -                                                              
        5  ---
        6  
        7  ## Quiz spec schema
        8  
       13 -<!-- What shape does a generated quiz take? Why those fields? 
          -What did you deliberately leave out? -->                      
        9 +The AI emits a single JSON object that validates against a Zod
          + schema variant chosen per quiz type. Three variants share a b
          +ase; they differ at the option and result level.              
       10  
       11 +```ts                                                         
       12 +{                                                             
       13 +  id: uuid,                          // stable across edits   
       14 +  type: "score" | "card" | "tag",    // immutable for an exist
          +ing quiz                                                      
       15 +  title: string,                                              
       16 +  description: string,                                        
       17 +  questions: [{                                               
       18 +    id: uuid,                                                 
       19 +    text: string,                                             
       20 +    type: "multiple_choice" | "select_multiple" | "slider",   
       21 +    position: number,                // explicit ordering, NOT
          + created_at                                                   
       22 +    options: [{                                               
       23 +      id: uuid,                                               
       24 +      text: string,                                           
       25 +      position: number,                                       
       26 +      score?: number,                // present for score/card
          +; absent for tag                                              
       27 +      tags?: string[],               // present for tag; absen
          +t for score/card                                              
       28 +    }]                                                        
       29 +  }],                                                         
       30 +  results: [{                                                 
       31 +    id: uuid,                                                 
       32 +    title_text: string,                                       
       33 +    description: string,                                      
       34 +    cta_text: string,                                         
       35 +    cta_url: string (URL),                                    
       36 +    range: [number, number],         // [lo, hi] inclusive    
       37 +  }]   // empty for tag quizzes                               
       38 +}                                                             
       39 +```                                                           
       40 +                                                              
       41 +**Why these fields, not others:**                             
       42 +                                                              
       43 +- **Three quiz types instead of one polymorphic shape**: the r
          +esult-screen logic and the AI's prompt vary so meaningfully ac
          +ross "score with bucketed results", "shareable badge", and "ta
          +g tally" that a single mega-schema would have given the model 
          +too many ways to be wrong. Three small schemas ‚Üí three smaller
          + prompt surfaces ‚Üí fewer retries.                             
       44 +- **`position` int instead of "ordered by `created_at`"**: the
          + original spec ordered questions by created_at, but that fight
          +s you the second the user reorders during an edit (you'd have 
          +to fake timestamps). Explicit position means edits are obvious
          + and `created_at` keeps meaning "when this row was made."     
       45 +- **`range_lo` / `range_hi` columns instead of `range numeric[
          +2]`**: makes `score BETWEEN range_lo AND range_hi` index-frien
          +dly and lets Postgres enforce `range_lo <= range_hi` as a CHEC
          +K.                                                            
       46 +- **No branching**: scope-cut. Branching needs a graph schema 
          +and a runtime that can choose-your-own-adventure; given the ti
          +me budget I went additive-scoring-only.                       
       47 +                                                              
       48 +**Deliberately left out:**                                    
       49 +                                                              
       50 +- Question types beyond MC / select-multiple / slider (no free
          +-text, no image, no rating-scale).                            
       51 +- Per-option weighting beyond a flat `score` integer. (Equival
          +ent to "every question contributes equally"; weighted question
          +s can be encoded by giving heavier questions higher option sco
          +res.)                                                         
       52 +- Multiple result dimensions per quiz (e.g. axes like Big Five
          +). One axis only ‚ÄĒ score or tags.                             
       53 +- Branching, conditional questions, randomized question order 
          +at runtime.                                                   
       54 +                                                              
       55  ## LLM choice
       56  
       17 -<!-- Which provider and model did you use? Why? Cost-per-quiz 
          -estimate? -->                                                 
       57 +**Provider:** Anthropic. **Model:** `claude-sonnet-4-6` for bo
          +th create and edit, no escalation on retry.                   
       58  
       59 +**Why Sonnet 4.6 specifically:**                              
       60 +                                                              
       61 +- The structured-output surface (`messages.parse` + `zodOutput
          +Format`) is a native helper in the Anthropic SDK 0.90 ‚ÄĒ single
          + function call, automatic Zod validation, no manual JSON-extra
          +ction or `tool_use`-shaped boilerplate.                       
       62 +- Sonnet 4.6 is the right cost/quality tradeoff for "follow a 
          +tightly-defined schema and write friendly copy." Opus 4.7 woul
          +d be ~5√ó more per quiz with no schema-compliance gain on this 
          +task ‚ÄĒ generating quiz copy isn't reasoning-bound. I considere
          +d Opus-on-retry but that disappears once you decide not to ret
          +ry at all (see Prompt reliability below).                     
       63 +- The `output_config: { format: zodOutputFormat(schema) }` int
          +egration produces typed `parsed_output` directly ‚ÄĒ no second-p
          +ass parsing.                                                  
       64 +                                                              
       65 +**Cost per quiz** (Sonnet 4.6 list pricing: $3 / MTok input, $
          +15 / MTok output):                                            
       66 +                                                              
       67 +- **Create**: ~1,650 in + ~2,200 out ‚Üí **$0.038/call**        
       68 +- **Edit**: ~3,800 in + ~2,300 out ‚Üí **$0.046/call**          
       69 +- **Round number**: ~4¬Ę per generation, ~5¬Ę per edit. A creato
          +r iterating 5 times to land a quiz spends ~$0.25.             
       70 +                                                              
       71 +System prompt is ~1,500 tokens. The biggest cost lever I'd pul
          +l next is prompt caching the system prompt (it's identical for
          + every create call) ‚ÄĒ Anthropic supports `cache_control` and w
          +ould save ~90% of input cost.                                 
       72 +                                                              
       73  ## Question type vocabulary
       74  
       21 -<!-- Which question types does your system support? Which did 
          -you skip and why? -->                                         
       75 +Three components, all share `(question, options, onAnswer, pen
          +ding)` props:                                                 
       76  
       77 +- **`multiple_choice`** ‚ÄĒ tile grid, single click advances. St
          +ored as `option_chosen_id`.                                   
       78 +- **`select_multiple`** ‚ÄĒ tile grid with checkbox affordance, 
          +Continue button enables when ‚Č•1 selected. Sums scores / unions
          + tags. Stored as `selected_option_ids uuid[]`.                
       79 +- **`slider`** ‚ÄĒ native range input styled olive, value bubble
          + above thumb, 0 ‚Üí max(option.score). Stored as `numeric_answer
          + int`.                                                        
       80 +                                                              
       81 +A CHECK constraint on `questions_answered` enforces exactly on
          +e of those three columns is non-null per row.                 
       82 +                                                              
       83 +**Skipped:**                                                  
       84 +                                                              
       85 +- **Free-text input** ‚ÄĒ no good way to score it without anothe
          +r LLM call at take time, which is expensive and slow.         
       86 +- **Image-pick** ‚ÄĒ needs an asset pipeline; out of scope.     
       87 +- **Yes/no** ‚ÄĒ degenerate case of multiple_choice.            
       88 +- **Rating scale** ‚ÄĒ slider covers it.                        
       89 +                                                              
       90  ## Scoring & results logic
       91  
       25 -<!-- How does scoring work? Weighting? Branching? Multiple res
          -ult dimensions? What's in vs. out of scope? -->               
       92 +**Score quizzes**: every chosen option's `score` (or every sel
          +ected option's score for select-multiple, or the slider's nume
          +ric value) sums into a total. The total is bucketed against th
          +e `results` table's `range_lo .. range_hi` to pick the title/d
          +escription/CTA shown.                                         
       93  
       94 +**Card quizzes**: identical math under the hood. The result te
          +xt comes from the matched bucket; the *visual* is a randomly c
          +hosen olive-gold badge SVG (3 hand-drawn variants, picked by h
          +ashing the session ID so refreshes are stable). Decision #6/9c
          +/20 in the convo: "card quiz will basically be the same as sco
          +re, but depending on the score it shows a certain card. note t
          +his in decisions as a simplicity measure."                    
       95 +                                                              
       96 +**Tag quizzes**: every option carries `tags string[]`. We tall
          +y tags across the user's answers; the result screen shows the 
          +top tags with counts. No `results` table rows.                
       97 +                                                              
       98 +**Validators that go beyond Zod shape** (post-parse, throw `Qu
          +izValidationError`):                                          
       99 +                                                              
      100 +- non-slider questions have ‚Č•2 options; slider questions have 
          +exactly 1                                                     
      101 +- score/card result ranges cover `[0, max_possible_score]` wit
          +h no gaps and no overlaps (sorted, first range starts at 0, ea
          +ch next `range[0] === prev[1] + 1`, last `range[1] >= maxScore
          +`)                                                            
      102 +- card needs ‚Č•1 result; tag needs 0 results; all CTA URLs pars
          +e via `new URL()`                                             
      103 +- IDs are unique within a quiz                                
      104 +                                                              
      105 +These checks run server-side in `lib/ai/validators.ts` and sur
          +face as 422 on the route handlers.                            
      106 +                                                              
      107 +**Out of scope** (deliberate):                                
      108 +                                                              
      109 +- Weighted questions (you can simulate by raising option score
          +s).                                                           
      110 +- Multi-axis results (e.g. one tag-axis + one score-axis on th
          +e same quiz).                                                 
      111 +- Branching: question N depends on answer to question N-1.    
      112 +- Adaptive scoring (e.g. confidence-weighted).                
      113 +                                                              
      114  ## Edit loop
      115  
       29 -<!-- After the first generation, how does a user iterate? Full
          - regeneration, spec patching, or direct editing? Why? -->     
      116 +The user has **two simultaneous editors** on `/quiz/[id]/edit`
          +:                                                             
      117  
      118 +1. **Direct JSON editing** in a textarea. Save validates again
          +st the same Zod + post-parse validators as the AI path before 
          +persisting. Bad JSON ‚Üí `alert()` per locked decision #8.      
      119 +2. **AI editing** in a prompt box ("add a question about X", "
          +make the results funnier"). Sonnet 4.6 receives the *current q
          +uiz JSON* + the user's instruction and returns a **full update
          +d quiz JSON** ‚ÄĒ not a patch. We then diff it against the curre
          +nt rows server-side using a plpgsql function called `apply_qui
          +z_diff(jsonb)`.                                               
      120 +                                                              
      121 +**Why full-replacement instead of JSON patches:**             
      122 +                                                              
      123 +- Anthropic's structured output is a sweet spot for "produce a
          + complete object that matches a schema." Asking for a JSON Pat
          +ch ("op": "add", "path": "...") is doable but doubles the prom
          +pt complexity and gives the model more ways to be wrong. Net c
          +ost is similar (the new quiz JSON is roughly the same size as 
          +a patch + context).                                           
      124 +- The diff is computed *server-side* via `apply_quiz_diff` (on
          +e Postgres function call) ‚ÄĒ UPSERTs by id, hard-deletes childr
          +en whose ids are absent. The model just has to emit the full n
          +ew state.                                                     
      125 +                                                              
      126 +**Why this preserves IDs across edits:**                      
      127 +                                                              
      128 +- The system prompt explicitly tells the model to **preserve U
          +UIDs for items it kept**. We then back this up server-side: `n
          +ormalizeIdsForEdit` walks the new quiz alongside the original,
          + keeps any AI-supplied id that matches a known original, and m
          +ints a fresh `crypto.randomUUID()` for genuinely new items. So
          + even when the model invents bad IDs for new items, the persis
          +tence layer always passes Postgres-valid UUIDs to `apply_quiz_
          +diff` and stable rows update in place instead of being deleted
          +-and-reinserted.                                              
      129 +                                                              
      130 +**No snapshots:** the editor shows a warning banner ‚ÄĒ edits th
          +at remove a question cascade-delete the historical answers for
          + that question. This was a locked decision (the trade-off for 
          +keeping the schema simple). For breaking changes, the recommen
          +dation in the banner is "create a new quiz."                  
      131 +                                                              
      132  ## Prompt reliability
      133  
       33 -<!-- How do you validate LLM output? Retries? Fallbacks? What 
          -happens when it returns garbage? -->                          
      134 +Three layers of validation, in this order:                    
      135  
      136 +1. **Anthropic structured output** (`messages.parse` + `zodOut
          +putFormat(schema)`) ‚ÄĒ the model is constrained to JSON conform
          +ing to the Zod-derived JSON Schema. The SDK auto-validates and
          + throws if parse fails.                                       
      137 +2. **Post-parse semantic validators** (`lib/ai/validators.ts`)
          + ‚ÄĒ option counts, score-range coverage, URL validity, ID uniqu
          +eness. These can't be expressed in JSON Schema and run after p
          +arse succeeds.                                                
      138 +3. **Postgres constraints** ‚ÄĒ UUID format, FK integrity, the `
          +exactly_one_answer` CHECK on `questions_answered`, the `result
          +_range_valid` CHECK.                                          
      139 +                                                              
      140 +**On failure: no retries, just `alert()`.** Locked decision #8
          + in the convo. The reasoning: in the demo audience (a technica
          +l user playing with the tool), a fast failure with a specific 
          +error message ("AI returned an invalid spec ‚ÄĒ Result ranges ha
          +ve a gap between [0,5] and [7,10]") is more actionable than si
          +lently retrying 3√ó and either delivering inconsistent results 
          +or wasting 30s on the wheel. The Anthropic SDK is configured w
          +ith `maxRetries: 0` to make this explicit.                    
      141 +                                                              
      142 +For a production audience with non-technical users, you'd want
          + at least one transparent retry ‚ÄĒ preferably *with the prior e
          +rror appended to the prompt* so the model has context on what 
          +to fix. That's the obvious next move.                         
      143 +                                                              
      144  ## Data model
      145  
       37 -<!-- How are quizzes and responses stored? What does the quiz-
          -creator dashboard actually show? -->                          
      146 +Seven tables, all FK-cascaded:                                
      147  
      148 +```                                                           
      149 +quiz (id, type, title, description, created_at, updated_at)   
      150 +  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ question (id, quiz_id, text, type, position, ...)       
      151 +        ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ option (id, question_id, text, score?, tags[], pos
          +ition, ...)                                                   
      152 +  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ result (id, quiz_id, title_text, description, cta_text, 
          +cta_url,                                                      
      153 +              range_lo, range_hi, ...)                        
      154 +                                                              
      155 +session (id, quiz_id, start_time, end_time?, device, browser, 
          +referrer, user_agent)                                         
      156 +  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ questions_answered (id, session_id, question_id,        
      157 +                          option_chosen_id? | numeric_answer? 
          +| selected_option_ids[]?,                                     
      158 +                          answered_at, ...)                   
      159 +  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ result_screen_clicked (id, session_id, result_id, create
          +d_at)                                                         
      160 +```                                                           
      161 +                                                              
      162 +**The CHECK on `questions_answered`** enforces that *exactly o
          +ne* of `option_chosen_id`, `numeric_answer`, `selected_option_
          +ids` is set per row ‚ÄĒ so the renderer, the analytics queries, 
          +and the type system all agree on what kind of answer they're l
          +ooking at.                                                    
      163 +                                                              
      164 +**`session_outcome` view** computes `total_score` and `tag_cou
          +nts (jsonb)` per session by joining session ‚Üí questions_answer
          +ed ‚Üí option (and unioning slider numeric values). This is the 
          +"compute on read" approach (locked decision #1) ‚ÄĒ no derived `
          +session_outcomes` table to keep in sync. The view caught a rea
          +l bug during smoke testing: a naive `lateral unnest(tags)` cro
          +ss-joined with score contributions, dropping every score row w
          +hen tags were empty arrays. The fix splits score and tag aggre
          +gations into separate CTEs and joins them at the top level.   
      165 +                                                              
      166 +**`apply_quiz_diff(p_quiz jsonb)`** is the single SQL function
          + used for both create and edit persistence: UPSERT by id, then
          + delete child rows whose ids aren't in the input. This gives t
          +rue atomicity in one round-trip ‚ÄĒ supabase-js doesn't expose P
          +ostgres transactions, so without this function an edit could h
          +alf-apply on network failure.                                 
      167 +                                                              
      168 +**Tracking** per locked decision #7: `device`, `browser`, `ref
          +errer`, `user_agent` columns directly on `session`. Captured c
          +lient-side in `lib/client-meta.ts` from `navigator.userAgent` 
          +(lightweight regex, no UA-parser dependency) and `document.ref
          +errer` (with same-origin filtering so internal navigation does
          +n't pollute traffic stats), passed to the `startSession` Serve
          +r Action.                                                     
      169 +                                                              
      170 +**The dashboard shows:**                                      
      171 +                                                              
      172 +- Top stats: total quizzes, total sessions, completion rate (a
          +cross all quizzes), the worst-performing quiz by incompletion 
          +rate (live calc, no minimum-N threshold per locked decision #1
          +6 ‚ÄĒ for the demo we want the data point even on tiny samples).
      173 +- Quiz grid with type-pill, question count, sessions started/c
          +ompleted, Take/Stats/Edit links.                              
      174 +- Per-quiz stats: 4-tile top stats (Started/Completed/Completi
          +on%/Q count), funnel by question reached, avg time per questio
          +n, type-specific panel (score = histogram + bucket distributio
          +n; card = same; tag = per-tag counts + drop-off-by-tag), devic
          +e/browser/referrer breakdown, recent sessions list with `?sess
          +ion=` deep-dive that filters every chart to a single session a
          +nd shows the per-answer trace.                                
      175 +                                                              
      176  ## Cost
      177  
       41 -<!-- Approximate $ per generated quiz. Show your math. -->    
      178 +Sonnet 4.6 list pricing as of April 2026: **$3 / MTok input**,
          + **$15 / MTok output**.                                       
      179  
      180 +**Per-create breakdown:**                                     
      181 +                                                              
      182 +- System prompt: ~1,500 input tokens (shared rules + per-type 
          +rules + 1-2 few-shot examples)                                
      183 +- User prompt: ~150 input tokens (the description)            
      184 +- Schema definition (sent as part of the structured-output con
          +fig): minimal; included in system overhead                    
      185 +- Output: 8-question quiz with 4 options each + 4 result tiers
          + ‚Čą 2,200 output tokens                                        
      186 +                                                              
      187 +‚Üí **0.00165 √ó $3 + 0.0022 √ó $15 ‚Čą $0.0379 per create**, call i
          +t **~$0.04**.                                                 
      188 +                                                              
      189 +**Per-edit breakdown:**                                       
      190 +                                                              
      191 +- System prompt: ~1,500                                       
      192 +- Current quiz JSON: ~2,200                                   
      193 +- Edit instruction: ~80                                       
      194 +- Output: ~2,300                                              
      195 +                                                              
      196 +‚Üí **0.0038 √ó $3 + 0.0023 √ó $15 ‚Čą $0.0459 per edit**, call it *
          +*~$0.05**.                                                    
      197 +                                                              
      198 +A creator iterating 5 times to land a quiz: ~25¬Ę. Generating 1
          +,000 quizzes: $40 in tokens. Cheapest improvement at scale: **
          +prompt-cache the system prompt** (saves ~90% of input cost sin
          +ce the system block is identical across calls) ‚ÄĒ Anthropic SDK
          + supports `cache_control: { type: 'ephemeral' }` on the system
          + block. Not implemented in this MVP because cost wasn't a cons
          +traint at this stage.                                         
      199 +                                                              
      200  ## What I'd do differently with more time
      201  
       45 -<!-- Honest list. -->                                         
      202 +- **Prompt caching on the system block** (90% input cost savin
          +gs, ~5 minutes to add).                                       
      203 +- **Retries with error-feedback** instead of fast-fail: when t
          +he validators throw, send the error message back to the model 
          +and ask it to fix. Better UX for non-technical users; slightly
          + more cost. The current fast-fail is right for a demo, not for
          + prod.                                                        
      204 +- **Versioned quizzes** (`quiz_version` row, sessions FK to a 
          +version): solves the "edits invalidate historical stats" trade
          +-off cleanly. Not in this MVP because it doubles the data-mode
          +l size.                                                       
      205 +- **Shareable result OG images** via `next/og`: a per-session 
          +PNG that previews the matched result so social shares aren't j
          +ust naked URLs.                                               
      206 +- **"Why this result?" expandable** on the result screen: show
          + the score breakdown per question. Builds trust; exposes scori
          +ng bugs faster.                                               
      207 +- **Tag co-occurrence heatmap** in the tag panel: which tags t
          +end to appear together? Useful for personalization features th
          +at need orthogonal axes.                                      
      208 +- **Branching support**: question N+1 depends on answer to que
          +stion N. Needs a graph model and a runtime that can route ‚ÄĒ bi
          +gger lift but unlocks lead-gen funnels.                       
      209 +- **CSV export from the stats page** (one button, dump complet
          +ed sessions with answers). 30 minutes of work that pays off th
          +e moment a marketer wants to slice the data in a spreadsheet. 
      210 +- **Inline taker preview in the editor**: split the editor pan
          +e to show the live taker rendered from the current JSON withou
          +t saving. Round-trips iteration time.                         
      211 +- **Auth + multi-tenancy**: the current build is open ‚ÄĒ anyone
          + with the URL can see admin/stats. RLS + a real auth provider 
          +would gate edits and per-org data.                            
      212 +- **Better UA parsing**: today it's a 30-line regex. Swap for 
          +`ua-parser-js` if/when device/browser breakdowns become load-b
          +earing.                                                       
      213 +- **Streaming AI responses** for create: a 30s wait on the dia
          +log feels slow. Anthropic SDK streams `parsed_output` incremen
          +tally; you could show the title appear, then questions one by 
          +one.                                                          
      214 +- **A real chart library** (or hand-rolled SVG with axes/toolt
          +ips) for the score histogram. The current stacked-bar approach
          + is fine for the demo but doesn't scale past ~30 score values.
      215 +                                                              
      216 +## Why-this-not-that footnotes                                
      217 +                                                              
      218 +- **Why Anthropic SDK 0.90 over the OpenAI SDK + structured ou
          +tputs?** Both are good. I went Anthropic because (a) the assig
          +nment ships both keys and (b) `messages.parse` + `zodOutputFor
          +mat` is the cleanest API I've used for structured generation ‚ÄĒ
          + no `response_format: { type: 'json_schema' }` boilerplate, no
          + manual reparse, typed return.                                
      219 +- **Why Server Actions for session lifecycle, route handlers f
          +or AI calls?** The dialog-based AI invocation needs a fetch() 
          +with handle-able errors and a router.push on success ‚ÄĒ that's 
          +a Route Handler. Session start/answer/end happen inside a `use
          +Transition` and don't return data the client needs to render ‚ÄĒ
          + Server Actions are the right tool.                           
      220 +- **Why no `@supabase/ssr`?** No auth in MVP; service-role on 
          +server, anon on client is enough. Adding `@supabase/ssr` would
          + be three extra files for zero present-day value.             
      221 +- **Why hand-rolled SVG funnel + bars instead of Recharts?** F
          +unnel + simple horizontal bars need ~50 lines each. Recharts a
          +dds ~200kb to the bundle for one page. Worth it the moment we 
          +add a histogram with axes/legends/tooltips.                   
      222 +- **Why a single olive aesthetic across admin AND taker?** Loc
          +ked decision #19 ‚ÄĒ the screenshot is the visual north star for
          + the whole app. The screenshot's sky/clouds/rolling-hills feel
          + translates surprisingly well to a dashboard once the chart de
          +nsity stays low. If the dashboard had to show 20 widgets per r
          +ow I'd revisit.                                               
      223 +- **Why does the editor have a JSON textarea, not a structured
          + form?** Power users reach for JSON; the structured-form alter
          +native is much more code. The schema-docs panel beside the edi
          +tor explains the shape so the JSON path stays approachable.

          +n and a per-answer trace appears.                             
       62  
       73 -# 2. Generate a migration from the diff                       
       74 -pnpm supabase db diff -f add_quizzes                          
       63 +### `/api/ai/create` and `/api/ai/edit`                       
       64 +- `POST` route handlers. Sonnet 4.6 with `client.messages.pars
          +e({ output_config: { format: zodOutputFormat(schema) } })`.   
       65 +- `maxRetries: 0` ‚ÄĒ fast fail, surface validator errors as 422
          + with a human-readable message that the client `alert()`s. (Se
          +e DECISIONS for the rationale.)                               
       66  
       76 -# 3. Apply locally                                            
       77 -pnpm supabase db reset                                        
       78 -```                                                           
       79 -                                                              
       80 -> `supabase db reset` drops the local DB and replays all migra
          -tions in order. Good for getting to a clean state.

      119 +                                                              
      120 +- **Next.js 16.2.4** (App Router, async params, Server Actions
          +, Route Handlers)                                             
      121 +- **React 19.2** (`useActionState`, `useTransition`)          
      122 +- **Tailwind v4** + **shadcn/ui** (base-nova) + custom olive p
          +alette in `globals.css`                                       
      123 +- **Anthropic SDK 0.90** with the `zodOutputFormat` helper for
          + structured generation                                        
      124 +- **Supabase JS 2.104** (service-role on server, anon on brows
          +er; no `@supabase/ssr` for MVP)                               
      125 +- **Zod 4** for schemas                                       
      126 +- **Postgres 17** (local Supabase) with a plpgsql `apply_quiz_
          +diff(jsonb)` for atomic create+edit persistence

      110 -## A note on AI tooling                                       
      130 +## What's not in the box                                      
      131  
      112 -Use whatever helps you ship. We use Claude Code at Olive. What
          - matters is the product decisions, not whether you typed every
          - character yourself.                                          
      132 +Per the kill list in the build plan: no auth/RLS, no quiz vers
          +ioning, no soft-delete, no branching logic, no free-text or im
          +age questions, no mid-quiz resume across sessions, no A/B, no 
          +embeddable widget, no per-quiz custom theming, no unit tests (
          +manual smoke only). See [`DECISIONS.md`](./DECISIONS.md) for "
          +what I'd do differently with more time."

‚Źļ All 8 phases shipped. Full build, every route returns 200 across all 3 quiz
  types, seed data is reproducible.

  What landed

  21 atomic commits from chore: env validation to chore(env): use z.url(). Every
   commit is self-explanatory.

  Routes (all 200 OK):
  - / ‚ÄĒ admin dashboard
  - /quiz/[id] ‚ÄĒ public taker (3 question types √ó 3 result types)
  - /quiz/[id]/edit ‚ÄĒ JSON + AI editor with schema docs + warning
  - /quiz/[id]/stats (+ ?session= deep-dive) ‚ÄĒ funnel, timing, per-type panels,
  sessions list
  - /api/ai/{create,edit} ‚ÄĒ Sonnet 4.6 with messages.parse + Zod-derived
  structured output

  Seeded examples (visible at / after pnpm supabase db reset):
  - Score: Are You Eating Too Much Ultra-Processed Food?
  - Tag: Let's personalize your Olive experience ūüęí
  - Card: What Kind of Eater Are You?
  - Each has 8 simulated sessions (6 completed, 2 abandoned) so the
  dashboard/stats look populated immediately.

  Cost on Sonnet 4.6: ~4¬Ę/create, ~5¬Ę/edit (math in DECISIONS.md).

  Files for you to see/own:
  - DECISIONS.md ‚ÄĒ you've written your own version (kept as-is)
  - ai/docs/plan.md ‚ÄĒ the phased build plan we executed
  - README.md ‚ÄĒ quick-start, layout, stack, kill-list pointer

  Notes on a couple of mid-build saves:
  - The session_outcome view had a lateral unnest(tags) cross-join bug that
  nuked score contributions when tag arrays were empty ‚ÄĒ caught in the Phase 4
  smoke test, fixed in 9e266a4 (separate score + tag aggregations, joined at the
   top).
  - Anthropic's structured output strips Zod regex/format constraints down to
  bare {type:"string"}, so the model produced inconsistent UUID strings.
  Switched to no-format-at-schema-level + server-side ID normalization
  (normalizeIdsForCreate mints fresh UUIDs; normalizeIdsForEdit preserves IDs
  that match originals so apply_quiz_diff updates rows in place). Fixed in
  c2d0c7d.

  Dev server + Supabase are still running. To take a quiz in the browser:
  http://localhost:3000.

  Fixes I'm landing now (in priority order)

  1. Time-per-question final-question math (headline analytics bug ‚ÄĒ every stats
   page is wrong)
  2. Lint failure in ResultCard (blocks CI)
  3. javascript: URL hole in validator (security)
  4. Card-with-0-results TypeError in validator (minor)
  5. Server Action authorization (question/result must belong to the session's
  quiz)
  6. CTA click rate could exceed 100% (UNIQUE constraint + distinct count)
  7. N+1 dashboard queries (perf at modest scale)
  8. parseReferrer leaks raw URL; iPad mis-classified as Desktop

  Starting with #1 + #2.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Fix #1 + #2 ‚ÄĒ time-per-question math + ResultCard lint

‚Źļ Update(lib/analytics-queries.ts)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 16 lines, removed 12 lines
      171    }
      172  
      173    // For each question, collect the per-session time spent on 
           it.
      174 +  // Locked decision #17:                                     
      175 +  //   - Q1 time: q1.answered - session.start                 
      176 +  //   - Middle: q[i].answered - q[i-1].answered              
      177 +  //   - Final question of the QUIZ when this session complete
          +d: end - q.answered                                           
      178 +  //   - Final question of the QUIZ when this session abandone
          +d: excluded                                                   
      179 +  // A session's last *answered* question is only treated as t
          +he "final" question                                           
      180 +  // when arr.length === questions.length AND end_time is set.
          + For abandoned                                                
      181 +  // sessions, every answered question still gets the normal c
          +ur-prev measurement.                                          
      182    const buckets = new Map<string, number[]>();
      183 +  const totalQuestions = questions.length;                    
      184    for (const [sid, arr] of bySession) {
      185      const sess = sessionMap.get(sid);
      186      if (!sess) continue;
      187      const startMs = new Date(sess.start_time).getTime();
      188      const endMs = sess.end_time ? new Date(sess.end_time).getT
           ime() : null;
      189 +    const completed = arr.length === totalQuestions && endMs !
          += null;

       22 + */                                                           
       23 +async function getQuizSessionCounts(): Promise<               
       24 +  Map<string, { started: number; completed: number }>         
       25 +> {                                                           
       26 +  const supabase = getServerClient();                         
       27 +  const counts = new Map<string, { started: number; completed:
          + number }>();                                                 
       28 +  // Page through in case there are many sessions; cap at 100k
          + for safety.                                                  
       29 +  const PAGE = 1000;                                          
       30 +  for (let from = 0; from < 100_000; from += PAGE) {          
       31 +    const { data, error } = await supabase                    
       32 +      .from("session")                                        
       33 +      .select("quiz_id, end_time")                            
       34 +      .range(from, from + PAGE - 1);                          
       35 +    if (error) throw new Error(error.message);                
       36 +    if (!data || data.length === 0) break;                    
       37 +    for (const row of data) {                                 
       38 +      const cur = counts.get(row.quiz_id) ?? { started: 0, com
          +pleted: 0 };                                                  
       39 +      cur.started += 1;                                       
       40 +      if (row.end_time != null) cur.completed += 1;           
       41 +      counts.set(row.quiz_id, cur);                           
       42 +    }                                                         
       43 +    if (data.length < PAGE) break;                            
       44 +  }                                                           
       45 +  return counts;                                              
       46 +}                                                             
       47 +

          +mber>> {

  Fixes shipped (8 commits)

  1. fix(stats,lint) ‚ÄĒ Final-question time math now (end - cur) instead of (end 
  - prev). Verified: Q1=5s, Q2=7s, Q3=10s in a controlled scenario (was Q3=18s).
   Plus React lint fix on ResultCard.
  2. fix(security) ‚ÄĒ Validator now rejects javascript:/data: CTA URLs (XSS
  hole). Card-with-0-results no longer throws TypeError.
  3. fix(stats) ‚ÄĒ UNIQUE(session_id, result_id) on result_screen_clicked so
  re-clicks can't inflate CTA rate above 100%. Defensive Math.min(100, ...) cap
  on the displayed percentage.
  4. fix(security,actions) ‚ÄĒ Server Actions now authorize: questions/results
  must belong to the session's quiz. Client meta strings clipped to 500 chars.
  CTA re-click is idempotent (catches 23505 unique-violation).
  5. perf(dashboard) ‚ÄĒ Replaced N+1 count queries (was 500+ on 100 quizzes) with
   two paged scans + JS aggregation. Verified identical numbers (3 quizzes / 24
  sessions / 75% / 6-of-8 per quiz).
  6. fix(client-meta) ‚ÄĒ iPadOS 13+ now detected as Tablet; failed-parse referrer
   returns "(other)" instead of leaking the raw URL.

  What I deliberately didn't fix

  - No-auth admin ‚ÄĒ locked decision #7, documented in DECISIONS.
  - alert() on AI failure ‚ÄĒ locked decision #8, documented.
  - Hard cascade delete on edit ‚ÄĒ locked decision #5, documented in DECISIONS +
  warning banner.

  useful add but additive scope; left for the "if time permits" list.
  - Above-spec wins flagged by Spec audit (Share button, SessionDeepDive, AI
  ID-rewrite, drop-off-by-tag, schema-aware editor docs) ‚ÄĒ already in.

      484  
      701 -## Constraints and reminders for the browser AI               
      485 +## Part 7 ‚ÄĒ Notes for the executor                            
      486  
      703 -- **Do not assume client-side routing.** The app uses Next.js 
          -16 server components in many places ‚ÄĒ page transitions may inv
          -olve full server fetches. Wait on `domcontentloaded` for navig
          -ations.                                                       
      704 -- **Wait long enough for AI calls.** Sonnet 4.6 generation can
          - take 15‚Äď40s for create, similar for edit. Set per-action time
          -outs to **60s** before declaring failure.                     
      705 -- **Do not rely on test IDs.** The app does not currently expo
          -se `data-testid` attributes ‚ÄĒ match by visible text, role, ARI
          -A label, and structural CSS classes (e.g. `olive-tile`).      
      706 -- **`alert()` is the error path.** If any scenario triggers a 
          -`window.alert(...)`, capture the message verbatim ‚ÄĒ those mess
          -ages start with strings like `"AI returned an invalid spec ‚ÄĒ"`
          -, `"Couldn't generate the quiz."`, `"Couldn't reach the server
          -: ‚Ä¶"`. Treat any alert during a happy-path scenario as a **FAI
          -L** for that scenario.                                        
      707 -- **Background:** the SkyHillsBackground is `position: fixed; 
          -z-index: -10` ‚ÄĒ it lives behind every page. Don't expect it to
          - scroll with the content.                                     
      708 -- **Keep cleanup in mind.** Scenario 7 mutates a seeded quiz t
          -itle; revert it.                                              
      487 +- **Take quizzes don't require any particular answer pattern**
          + ‚ÄĒ pick whatever's easy. The point is exercising the flow, not
          + landing in a specific result bucket.                         
      488 +- **AI calls genuinely take 15-60 seconds** ‚ÄĒ don't time out a
          +t 30s, wait the full 60s.                                     
      489 +- **Errors surface as `window.alert()` dialogs** ‚ÄĒ by design (
          +it's a known design choice). If you see one, capture the messa
          +ge text but don't treat it as a crash; document it as a scenar
          +io failure.                                                   
      490 +- **No login or signup** ‚ÄĒ the entire app is open. There's no 
          +auth-related path to test.                                    
      491 +- **The DB has 3 quizzes seeded** ‚ÄĒ don't expect to find other
          +s unless you create them in Scenario 6.                       
      492 +- **You can leave the new quiz from Scenario 6 in the DB** ‚ÄĒ t
          +hat's fine, no cleanup expected.                              
      493 +- **If something is so broken that a scenario can't proceed at
          + all, mark it FAIL with the blocker explained, then continue t
          +o the next scenario.**                                        
      494 +                                                              
      495 +Good luck. Be thorough, be honest, and screenshot generously.

‚Źļ Spec rewritten ‚ÄĒ 495 lines, 7 explicit parts, all 15 scenarios in the new
  structure, plus a verbatim reporting template.

  What's in the new spec

  Part 1 ‚ÄĒ What this project is (was missing). Three paragraphs explaining:
  Olive is a grocery scanner app; Quiz Studio is an internal tool to build quiz
  funnels (onboarding, lead gen, share quizzes); the app generates / hosts /
  tracks quizzes; and the three quiz types with what each result screen looks
  like.

  Part 2 ‚ÄĒ What pages exist and what they do (was missing). Conceptual tour of
  every page (/, /quiz/[id], /quiz/[id]/edit, /quiz/[id]/stats, ?session=
  deep-dive) ‚ÄĒ explains what each is for before listing what to test on it. So
  the AI knows that the editor is "where the admin tweaks an existing quiz" not
  just "a page with a textarea."

  Part 3 ‚ÄĒ What you have to start with. URL, the 3 seeded quiz IDs as a literal
  table with example URLs constructed for them, what's allowed and what to avoid
   (don't make >5 quizzes ‚ÄĒ costs $0.04 each).

  Part 4 ‚ÄĒ Visual aesthetic checklist. The 10-row table the previous spec had,
  plus a "red flags that mean something's broken" section so the AI knows what
  counts as a regression vs intentional design.

  Part 5 ‚ÄĒ Test scenarios. The 15 scenarios from before, kept tight.

  Part 6 ‚ÄĒ How to report back. A verbatim markdown template the AI must fill in,
   plus an A-F grading rubric anchored to "scenarios passed" + "visual checks" +
   "feels like a real product."

  Part 7 ‚ÄĒ Notes for the executor. Things that would otherwise trip up a
  context-less AI: AI calls take 15-60s (don't bail early); errors surface as
  alert() by design; no login; you can leave Scenario-6's test quiz behind; mark
   FAIL+continue if a scenario blocks.

  The spec is at /tmp/browser-test-spec.md ‚ÄĒ paste it directly into Browser Use,
   Playwright-MCP, Operator, or any other browser-controlling AI's prompt box.
  It's self-contained ‚ÄĒ no codebase access needed.

  Verdict: PASS                                                                 
  Evidence: All 7 expected sections present: header with Edit / Take it ‚Üó,      
  top-stat tiles (Started 9 / Completed 7 / Completion 78% / Questions 6),      
  funnel with vertical bars and "‚Üď2 dropped (22%)" label, avg time per question 
   with horizontal bars, Result distribution with 4 score-bucket rows, Score    
  histogram (avg 20.0), Headline numbers (7 completed, avg 20.0, CTA clicks 4   
  (57%)), Where they came from (Device/Browser/Referrer mini-bars), and Recent  
  sessions table with 9 rows. No NaN%, no broken charts.                        
                                                                                
  Scenario 10 ‚ÄĒ Click into a session deep-dive                                  
                                                                                
  Verdict: PASS                                                                 
  Evidence: Clicking "Open" on the first row navigated to                       
  /stats?session=9ccebaa8-‚Ä¶. "Clear filter" pill appeared in header (cream +    
  gold styling). Top tiles became 1 / 1 / 100% / 6. Subtitle changed to         
  "Filtered to one session ‚ÄĒ pick Clear in the row to see everyone." Funnel     
  showed all 1s. Session deep-dive panel rendered below the meta breakdown with 
   one trace card per question showing "Picked: ‚Ä¶", "+N score" and quiz-type    
  pill ("MULTIPLE CHOICE", "SELECT MULTIPLE", "SLIDER").                        
                                                                                
  Scenario 11 ‚ÄĒ Clear the deep-dive filter                                      
                                                                                
  Verdict: PASS                                                                 
  Evidence: Clicked "Clear filter" pill; URL reverted to exactly                
  /quiz/<id>/stats (no querystring); top stats reverted to 9/7/78%/6 (matching  
  Scenario 9).                                                                  
                                                                                
  Scenario 12 ‚ÄĒ Esc closes the create dialog                                    
                                                                                
  Verdict: PASS                                                                 
  Evidence: Opened dialog, pressed Escape, dialog closed with no AI call made.  
                                                                                
  Scenario 13 ‚ÄĒ Click outside the create dialog closes it                       
                                                                                
  Verdict: PASS                                                                 
  Evidence: Clicking the dimmed backdrop area (top-left of viewport) closed the 
   dialog. Subsequent click inside the dialog box (on the heading) left the     
  dialog open ‚ÄĒ confirming backdrop-only behavior is correct.                   
                                                                                
  Scenario 14 ‚ÄĒ Mobile viewport (375√ó812)                                       
                                                                                
  Verdict: PASS                                                                 
  Evidence: At ~371px inner width: top stats stacked into a 2-column grid; quiz 
   cards stacked into a single column with the plus tile first; header didn't   
  overflow (no horizontal scroll). On the score quiz taker at the same width:   
  title + description + Start button rendered cleanly inside the white tile     
  with sky/cloud/sun background still visible above and hills visible below.    
  Note: The resize_window automation tool needed an oversized outer width       
  (~750√ó950) to land on a ~371px inner viewport due to chrome/scrollbar         
  overhead ‚ÄĒ a tooling note, not an app issue.                                  
                                                                                
  Scenario 15 ‚ÄĒ Keyboard navigation                                             
                                                                                
  Verdict: PARTIAL                                                              
  Evidence: Visible focus rings appeared correctly when tabbing through: header 
   logo ‚Üí Dashboard nav link ‚Üí Needs-attention tile ‚Üí Create-new-quiz tile      
  (etc.). Pressing Enter on the focused plus tile opened the dialog. However,   
  after pressing Tab 5 times inside the open dialog, focus escaped to a "Take   
  ‚Üó" link in the underlying quiz card grid (verified via                        
  document.activeElement.closest('[role=dialog]') returning null). Per the      
  spec's own note: "no focus trap on dialog." Marking PARTIAL accordingly.      
                                                                                
  Visual aesthetic check                                                        
                                                                                
  Sky/cloud/hills background visible? YES ‚ÄĒ gradient + clouds + 3 hill          
  silhouettes + yellow sun glow on every page checked.                          
  Olive-deep green used for headings + primary buttons? YES ‚ÄĒ H1s, Start, Save, 
   Edit, "Try Olive‚Ä¶", and score circle all use the same #2F5D35-style          
  olive-deep green; no browser-default blue anywhere.                           
  Olive-gold badges on card quiz are hand-drawn, not stock? YES ‚ÄĒ saw the       
  hexagon variant with a clearly hand-drawn green olive-and-leaf shape inside a 
   golden hexagonal frame with subtle halo.                                     
  Any "NaN%" / "Infinity" / "undefined" rendered anywhere? NO                   
                                                                                
  Top 5 unexpected observations                                                 
                                                                                
  The score-quiz CTA opens https://olive.app/start, but that URL returns a 404  
  ("Page not found | Olive Technologies"). The spec said the CTA should land on 
   https://oliveapp.com/.... Either the spec is stale or the CTA target URL is  
  misconfigured ‚ÄĒ worth aligning.                                               
  The Score histogram chart on the stats page renders the 0‚Äď48 axis labels but  
  the bar area appeared visually empty even when filtered to a single session   
  with score 24 (the avg label "avg 24.0" updated correctly). The funnel and    
  result-distribution bars all rendered fine, so this looks specific to the     
  histogram component ‚ÄĒ possibly a dataset shape edge case rather than a hard   
  bug.                                                                          
  The card-quiz Share button gives no visible feedback after clicking. No       
  toast, no "Copied to clipboard" message appeared in the DOM. If the           
  implementation is "navigator.share fallback to clipboard," users on desktop   
  will be left wondering whether it worked.                                     
  After creating a new quiz in Scenario 6, the "needs attention" tile still     
  pointed at the original card quiz, but the new quiz already had STARTED 0 /   
  DONE ‚ÄĒ (em-dash) ‚ÄĒ that em-dash placeholder rendered nicely instead of "0%"   
  or "NaN%," which is a small but tasteful detail.                              
  Refreshing the card-quiz result screen always starts a brand-new session,     
  which makes the spec's "badge variant is stable across refresh" guarantee     
  untestable end-to-end from the user side. The variant may well be stable per  
  session-id, but there's no UI affordance to land on the same session's result 
   after a refresh, so users won't experience this stability either.

  Grade rationale                                                               
  14 of 15 scenarios PASS cleanly, the lone PARTIAL (Scenario 5) is explicitly  
  flagged as untestable in the brief itself, and Scenario 15's PARTIAL is a     
  known a11y gap. All visual checks are YES, no NaN/undefined/broken images,    
  every CTA, save, AI generation, AI edit, deep-dive filter, dialog             
  interaction, and mobile breakpoint behaved exactly as designed. The few rough 
   edges (CTA URL mismatch, silent Share button, visually empty histogram bars) 
   are cosmetic refinements rather than broken flows. This feels like a         
  polished, real product ‚ÄĒ earning an A.

  404. Re-seeding now.

‚Źļ Done. Dual-dimension model is live across the whole stack.

  What changed

  Schema: every option now requires both score: int ‚Č• 0 and tags: 
  string[].min(1) ‚ÄĒ replaced the separate scoreOption/tagOption with a single
  dualOption. All 3 quiz-type schemas use it.

  applies regardless of quiz type. Per-type rules reframed as "what drives the
  result screen" ‚ÄĒ they no longer instruct the model to omit one dimension.

  Persistence: quizFullToAIShape always emits both fields (was splitting on
  quiz.type).

  for every quiz type. Renders a PRIMARY panel (the dimension that drives the

  other dimension:

  - Card quiz ‚Üí CardPanel primary, TagPanel secondary
  - Tag quiz ‚Üí TagPanel primary, ScorePanel secondary

   explainer note about the dual-dimension model.

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 7m 52s

‚ĚĮ please add the correct rls / security policies to each table.                 

‚Źļ Right call. Currently the publishable (anon) key has implicit access to every
  table via the REST API ‚ÄĒ anyone with the URL could hit /rest/v1/quiz and read
  or even write rows. Locking it down with RLS now.

  The plan:
  - Enable RLS on all 7 tables ‚ÄĒ closed-by-default (no policies = all anon
  access denied)
  - Service-role continues to bypass RLS by design (that's how Postgres roles
  work) ‚ÄĒ so every Server Action and route handler keeps working unchanged,
  since they use the server client
  - Verify the lockdown: anon key ‚Üí no reads, no writes; service role ‚Üí
  unchanged

  This matches locked decision #7 (no auth, server-mediated) ‚ÄĒ the RLS just
  enforces the architectural rule at the DB layer instead of trusting the
  application layer alone.

  Listed 2 directories (ctrl+o to expand)

  Summary

  What landed:
  - supabase/schemas/90_rls/00_enable_rls.sql ‚ÄĒ enable row level security on all
   7 public tables with the threat-model rationale inline
  - supabase/schemas/90_rls/10_future_auth_templates.sql ‚ÄĒ commented-out policy
  templates for the post-auth scenario (creator-scoping,
  public-read-of-definitions, anonymous-taker writes) so the future-auth
  migration is a 10-minute job not a from-scratch design exercise
  - supabase/migrations/20260428001459_enable_rls.sql ‚ÄĒ auto-generated migration

  Why this design (rather than per-table SELECT/INSERT policies):
  - The MVP has zero browser-side database access ‚ÄĒ every read/write goes
  through the service-role client server-side. So opening up anon SELECT on quiz
   definitions would just be theoretical capability we don't use.
  - Closed-by-default is strictly safer: nothing leaks if a future engineer
  mistakenly tries to use the browser client directly.
  - When auth lands, the templates show exactly which 5-line policies to
  uncomment.

  Verified end-to-end:

  Service-role bypasses RLS by design ‚ÄĒ that's how Postgres roles work and why
  the entire app (Server Actions, route handlers, page server components) keeps
  working without any code changes. The RLS now enforces architecturally what
  the application layer already enforced procedurally: every database write must
   be mediated by server code that authorizes it.
